<div style="line-height: 1.6em; font-weight: bold;"><div>Episode 5</div></div>
<ul class="mw-collapsible-content" style="margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit; list-style: none; margin-left: 0;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> December 19, 2017</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Video_game_genre" title="Video game genre">Genre(s)</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Point-and-click" class="mw-redirect" title="Point-and-click">Point-and-click</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Mode(s)</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Single-player" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-player">Single-player</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i><b>Minecraft: Story Mode</b></i> is  an <a href="/wiki/Episodic_video_game" title="Episodic video game">episodic</a> <a href="/wiki/Point-and-click" class="mw-redirect" title="Point-and-click">point-and-click</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a> developed and published by <a href="/wiki/Telltale_Games" title="Telltale Games">Telltale Games</a>, based on <a href="/wiki/Mojang_Studios" title="Mojang Studios">Mojang Studios</a>' <a href="/wiki/Sandbox_video_game" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandbox video game">sandbox video game</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a></i>. The first five episodes were released between October 2015 through March 2016 and an additional three episodes were released as <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> (DLC) in mid-2016. A second season consisting of five episodes was released in 2017.
</p><p>The game follows the same episodic format as other Telltale Games titles, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Walking_Dead_(video_game_series)" title="The Walking Dead (video game series)">The Walking Dead</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wolf_Among_Us" title="The Wolf Among Us">The Wolf Among Us</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tales_from_the_Borderlands" title="Tales from the Borderlands">Tales from the Borderlands</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones_(2014_video_game)" title="Game of Thrones (2014 video game)">Game of Thrones</a></i>. The story revolves around a player-created character named Jesse, originally an <a href="/wiki/Everyman" title="Everyman">everyman</a>, who later becomes a hero together with their friends. During the first four episodes, Jesse and their friends attempt to reassemble an old group of heroes known as the Order of the Stone to save the Overworld from the destructive Wither Storm. The rest of the first season follows Jesse and their friends, now the new Order of the Stone, on a new adventure after discovering a powerful artifact. In the second season, Jesse faces the powerful Admin.
</p><p>The game was available for <a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Switch" title="Nintendo Switch">Nintendo Switch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a>. A retail version was released in December 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and the game's first season, excluding the DLC episodes, was released on <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> in late 2018. However, both seasons of the game became unplayable due to the closure of Telltale Games in late 2018, causing the game to be ultimately discontinued on June 25, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The Netflix release of the game was removed on December 5, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gameplay">Gameplay</span></h2>
<p><i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> is an <a href="/wiki/Episodic_video_game" title="Episodic video game">episodic</a> interactive comedy-drama <a href="/wiki/Point-and-click" class="mw-redirect" title="Point-and-click">point-and-click</a> <a href="/wiki/Graphic_adventure_game" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphic adventure game">graphic adventure</a> video game. It was released as a number of episodes similar to <a href="/wiki/Telltale_Games" title="Telltale Games">Telltale Games</a>' other games. Players can collect items, solve puzzles, and talk to non-player characters through <a href="/wiki/Conversation_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Conversation tree">conversation trees</a> to learn about the story and determine what to do next. Decisions that the player makes affect events in both the current episode and later episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> However, <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> is intended to be a <a href="/wiki/Family-friendly" title="Family-friendly">family-friendly</a> title, unlike Telltale's previous games, which tend to carry more mature or emotional overtones (including the death of major characters). As such, the decisions are intended to be pivotal and emotional but not to involve mature imagery or themes.<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Elements of crafting and building were included in the <a href="/wiki/Gameplay" title="Gameplay">gameplay</a> which are central to <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ign_pax_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign_pax-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The game includes combat and other action sequences, carried out through both <a href="/wiki/Quick_time_event" title="Quick time event">quick time events</a> and more arcade-like controls, such as steering around debris on a road.<sup id="cite_ref-ign_pax_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign_pax-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurogamer_firstlook_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogamer_firstlook-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The Netflix version of the first season (excluding the Adventure Pass episodes) was fully pre-rendered, using an enhanced version of the <a href="/wiki/Telltale_Tool" class="mw-redirect" title="Telltale Tool">Telltale Tool</a>, uses limited choices and the second version of male and female models, and re-created as an interactive series.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Setting">Setting</span></h3>
<p><i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> takes place in an interpretation of the world of <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a>,</i> known as the "Overworld", where the game is the extent of the characters' universe, and the characters are unaware that they are in a game.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The main character, Jesse, is an inexperienced resident of said universe who sets out on a journey with their friends within the world of <i>Minecraft</i> to find The Order of the Stone (Gabriel the Warrior, Ellegaard the Redstone Engineer, Magnus the Rogue, Soren the Architect and Ivor the Potion Brewer and Enchanter), five legendary adventurers who saved the <i>Minecraft</i> world.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_minecon_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_minecon-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The game includes settings that are normally difficult to access from within <i>Minecraft</i>, including the Nether and The End.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_minecon_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_minecon-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">Characters</span></h3>
<p>The player can customize Jesse, including choice of gender and skin tone. Jesse is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Patton_Oswalt" title="Patton Oswalt">Patton Oswalt</a> if male and by <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Taber" title="Catherine Taber">Catherine Taber</a> if female.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Other main characters within the <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> world include Jesse's friends Petra (voiced by <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Johnson_(actress)" title="Ashley Johnson (actress)">Ashley Johnson</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-ign_pax_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign_pax-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Axel (<a href="/wiki/Brian_Posehn" title="Brian Posehn">Brian Posehn</a>), Olivia (<a href="/wiki/Martha_Plimpton" title="Martha Plimpton">Martha Plimpton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natasha_Loring" title="Natasha Loring">Natasha Loring</a>), Lukas (<a href="/wiki/Scott_Porter" title="Scott Porter">Scott Porter</a>), and Jesse's pet pig, Reuben (<a href="/wiki/Dee_Bradley_Baker" title="Dee Bradley Baker">Dee Bradley Baker</a>). The first season features several characters in supporting roles, including the Order of the Stone—Gabriel (<a href="/wiki/Dave_Fennoy" title="Dave Fennoy">Dave Fennoy</a>), Magnus (<a href="/wiki/Corey_Feldman" title="Corey Feldman">Corey Feldman</a>), Ellegaard (<a href="/wiki/Grey_Griffin" class="mw-redirect" title="Grey Griffin">Grey Griffin</a>), Soren (<a href="/wiki/John_Hodgman" title="John Hodgman">John Hodgman</a>) and Ivor (<a href="/wiki/Paul_Reubens" title="Paul Reubens">Paul Reubens</a>), the latter of whom becomes a main character from episode five onwards—former Ocelot member and Blaze Rods leader Aiden (<a href="/wiki/Matthew_Mercer" title="Matthew Mercer">Matthew Mercer</a>); the ruler of Sky City, the Founder (<a href="/wiki/Melissa_Hutchison" title="Melissa Hutchison">Melissa Hutchison</a>); Milo (<a href="/wiki/Jim_Meskimen" title="Jim Meskimen">Jim Meskimen</a>), the leader of an underground building club; <i>Minecraft</i> <a href="/wiki/List_of_YouTubers" title="List of YouTubers">YouTubers</a> <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Maron" class="mw-redirect" title="Jordan Maron">CaptainSparklez</a>, <a href="/wiki/DanTDM" title="DanTDM">DanTDM</a>, LDShadowLady, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Garrett" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Garrett">Stampy Cat</a> and Stacy Plays (all played by themselves); Torque Dawg (<a href="/wiki/Adam_Harrington_(voice_actor)" title="Adam Harrington (voice actor)">Adam Harrington</a>); Cassie Rose/The White Pumpkin (<a href="/wiki/Ashly_Burch" title="Ashly Burch">Ashly Burch</a> with a disguised voice by <a href="/wiki/Roger_L._Jackson" title="Roger L. Jackson">Roger L. Jackson</a>); the super-computer PAMA (Jason 'jtop' Topolski); its creator and former Old Builder Harper (<a href="/wiki/Yvette_Nicole_Brown" title="Yvette Nicole Brown">Yvette Nicole Brown</a>); the warrior Emily (<a href="/wiki/Audrey_Wasilewski" title="Audrey Wasilewski">Audrey Wasilewski</a>); and the Old Builders—Hadrian (<a href="/wiki/Jim_Cummings" title="Jim Cummings">Jim Cummings</a>), Mevia (<a href="/wiki/Kari_Wahlgren" title="Kari Wahlgren">Kari Wahlgren</a>) and Otto (<a href="/wiki/Jamie_Alcroft" title="Jamie Alcroft">Jamie Alcroft</a>). Season 2 adds several more, such as Jesse's assistant Radar (<a href="/wiki/Yuri_Lowenthal" title="Yuri Lowenthal">Yuri Lowenthal</a>), the famous hero Jack (<a href="/wiki/Fred_Tatasciore" title="Fred Tatasciore">Fred Tatasciore</a>) and his villager sidekick Nurm (Mark Barbolak), Champion City ruler Stella (Ashley Albert) and her treasure sniffing llama Lluna, and the sinister Admin named Romeo (<a href="/wiki/JB_Blanc" title="JB Blanc">JB Blanc</a>).
</p><p>There are also several background characters, such as Maya, Ivy and a Fangirl (GK Bowes); Owen (Owen Hill); Gill (<a href="/wiki/Phil_LaMarr" title="Phil LaMarr">Phil LaMarr</a>); an EnderCon Usher named Reuben (also Jason 'jtop' Topolski); a Fanboy (Billy West); Lydia (Lydia Winters); and the EnderCon Building Competition Announcer (<a href="/wiki/Erin_Yvette" title="Erin Yvette">Erin Yvette</a>). Stauffer said that the human characters as a whole represent the different types of gamers who play <i>Minecraft</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_minecon_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_minecon-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Billy_West" title="Billy West">Billy West</a> narrates the first four episodes of the story.<sup id="cite_ref-ign_trailer_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign_trailer-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>This is a broad overview of the plot. Certain decisions made by the player will alter the details of specific events.
</p>
<h4><span id="Season_1_.282015.E2.80.9316.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_1_(2015–16)">Season 1 (2015–16)</span></h4>
<p>In a flashback, the Order of the Stone, consisting of Gabriel, Soren, Ivor, Ellegaard, and Magnus, defeats the Ender Dragon. In the present day, Jesse, his friends Axel and Olivia, and his pet pig Reuben prepare for the EnderCon building competition. The Ocelots, a rival team, attempt to sabotage their build, spooking Reuben. Jesse is attacked rescuing him but Petra saves them, who convinces Jesse to help her sell a Wither skull. The buyer, Ivor, tricks them and escapes with it. They pursue him and discover that Ivor plans to attack Gabriel using a Wither Storm. The group tries to stop it, but are unsuccessful. After recruiting Magnus and Ellegaard, they then head to Soren's lab, hoping that his Formidi-Bomb can destroy the Wither Storm, which Jesse uses, although either Magnus or Ellegaard dies in the process. However, the beast reforms in three clusters. The group, joined by Gabriel or Petra, escape. After that, Ivor takes the group to his lab to enchant a weapon which can destroy the Command Block. Jesse builds the enchanted weapon and destroys the command block, ultimately killing the Wither Storm, but not before the beast kills Reuben.
</p><p>Soon after, the group finds a Flint and Steel, which Ivor reveals that the "Old Builders" created it and supposedly the "Eversource", a chicken that lays spawn eggs. Jesse, Ivor, Lukas, and Petra return to the temple and opens a portal, leading them to Sky City. The group eventually finds the Eversource, but Aiden, the leader of a rival group called the Blaze Rods, steals it. Jesse defeats Aiden, who is imprisoned in the new Sky City.
</p><p>Jesse's group retrieve the Flint and Steel and try to return home through another portal, but find themselves in a portal-filled corridor. While travelling between them, they arrive in a graveyard with an invite to a supposed party in a nearby mansion, in which they meet others who were lured into it, among them Cassie Rose. After two of the mansion's residents are killed by traps, the group discovers that the culprit is Cassie, who is then defeated.
</p><p>Jesse and their companions meet the computer PAMA, which Jesse and Ivor escape from with aid by Harper, the scientist who created PAMA. She takes them to her lab to retrieve something to deactivate PAMA, where Jesse frees either Lukas or Petra before they are captured. Harper directs Jesse to PAMA's power source which they remove, freeing the other companion.
</p><p>Back in the portal corridor, Harper reveals the Atlas which can help Jesse's group return home. The Old Builders, consisting of Hadrian, Mevia, and Otto, imprison Jesse and force him to compete in games to win his friends' freedom, but Jesse makes a deal with Otto to free his friends, before battling and defeating Hadrian and Mevia, allowing them and the group to return home.
</p>
<h4><span id="Season_2_.282017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_2_(2017)">Season 2 (2017)</span></h4>
<p>Radar, Jesse's new assistant, notifies Jesse of an upcoming adventure with Petra. Jesse helps citizens prepare for Founding Day before meeting her. Their meeting place self-destructs to reveal a bottomless pit, where Jesse finds a mysterious gauntlet that gets stuck in their hand; but they manage to escape. Petra finds Jack, a hero who can help Jesse remove the gauntlet and the "heckmouth". Jack reveals that the gauntlet is tracked to an Ocean Monument, and that a "Structure Block" can close the pit. Jesse convinces Jack and his villager friend Nurm to take them and Petra to it. At the monument's centre, the Admin appears and attempts to kill them, but they and their companions escape to where Jesse collects a Structure Block and frees Jack's old friend Vos.
</p><p>After Jesse defeats it, the Admin returns and challenges Jesse's group to reclaim the clock (later destroyed by Jack or Petra) in his ice palace, who they then head towards, later joined by Stella and Lluna. However, Vos is revealed to have been the Admin the whole time, and he imprisons Jesse and the person who didn't destroy the clock, while the person who did gets the gauntlet transferred to their hand.
</p><p>Jesse resolves with their friends to find "Prisoner X", later revealed as Xara, who claims to knows how to escape the maze. Jesse opens their cell, but has to leave either Nurm or Lluna, a llama that they befriended, behind, before they combat whoever destroyed the clock and then with Xara, attack the Admin. Although it fails, they manage to free Petra or Jack from the Admin's control. The group escapes the prison with Radar in tow.
</p><p>Xara then shows them a portal which she re-powers, heading to an underground area below the bedrock. Jesse reunites with Ivor, who has become a ninja. Jesse learns more about the Admin, whose name is revealed to be Romeo, and that Romeo, Xara, and their friend Fred once were friends, but a disagreement led to Fred's death and Romeo's corruption. Jesse finds Xara's bed, and can choose to give it to her. Jesse then has to choose between saving either Radar or the people below the bedrock before escaping. 
</p><p>After returning home, Jesse, Petra, and Jack come up with a plan to battle Romeo. If Jesse gives Xara her bed, Romeo destroys the neighboring Champion City, but if Jesse didn't give Xara her bed, she attempts to attack Romeo only to get strangled to death. It is revealed that Ivor managed to free Nurm or Lluna from the prison. With Lukas's assistance, they arrive at the "Terminal Space", the home of the Admin. Jesse, Jack, and Petra reaches the Terminal Space, with Jesse collecting Fred's gauntlet and battling Romeo. Jesse successfully uses the gauntlet to strip Romeo of his power. Jesse then has a choice to either take Romeo back for redemption or leave him to his fate, and if they had chosen to rescue the people below the bedrock, then Radar arrives to save them; if not, Romeo distracts the monsters of Terminal Space for Jesse and their friends to escape. Jesse's final choice involves them either choosing to leave Beacontown and go on adventures with Petra, or staying as mayor.
</p>

<h3><span id="Season_1_.282015.E2.80.9316.29_2"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_1_(2015–16)_2">Season 1 (2015–16)</span></h3><p>
The main <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> game was separated into five episodes for its first season, released in one month intervals. Three additional episodes were later released.</p><table class="wikitable plainrowheaders wikiepisodetable" style="width:100%"><tbody><tr style="color:black;text-align:center"><th scope="col" style="background:#3B9FD4;width:5%"><abbr title="Number">No.</abbr><br />overall</th><th scope="col" style="background:#3B9FD4;width:5%"><abbr title="Number">No.</abbr> in<br />season</th><th scope="col" style="background:#3B9FD4">Title</th><th scope="col" style="background:#3B9FD4">Directed by</th><th scope="col" style="background:#3B9FD4">Written by</th><th scope="col" style="background:#3B9FD4">Original release date</th></tr><tr class="vevent" style="text-align:center;background:#F2F2F2"><th scope="row" rowspan="1" id="ep1" style="text-align:center">1</th><td style="text-align:center">1</td><td class="summary" rowspan="1" style="text-align:left">"The Order of the Stone"</td><td style="text-align:center">Dennis Lenart and Graham Ross</td><td style="text-align:center">Michael Choung and Laura Jacqmin</td><td style="text-align:center">October&#160;13,&#160;2015<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated itvstart">2015-10-13</span>)</span><sup id="cite_ref-Episode_1_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Episode_1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="expand-child"><td class="description" colspan="7" style="border-bottom:solid 3px #3B9FD4">

<h3><span id="Season_2_.282017.29_2"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_2_(2017)_2">Season 2 (2017)</span></h3>
<p>In July 2017, the first trailer was released for the second season, along with a release date of July 11.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_and_releases">Development and releases</span></h2>
<p>The idea for <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> came around the end of 2012 when <a href="/wiki/Telltale_Games" title="Telltale Games">Telltale Games</a> was engaged in work for <i><a href="/wiki/Tales_from_the_Borderlands" title="Tales from the Borderlands">Tales from the Borderlands</a></i>, an episodic series based on the <i><a href="/wiki/Borderlands_(series)" title="Borderlands (series)">Borderlands</a></i> series. The idea of developing stories around other established video game franchises led the team to brainstorm the idea for a <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a></i>-related game, given that the game was essentially a "blank canvas" for storytelling, according to Job Stauffer, and would create an interesting challenge.<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The two groups recognized the amount of fan-generated narrative content that existed in the way of <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> videos and other media forms that demonstrated the potential for storytelling in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-gamasutra_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Many on Telltale's staff were also already fans of <i>Minecraft</i>, with a private server that they played on, with some of the incidents that occurred on there becoming ideas for the game's story.<sup id="cite_ref-gamasutra_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Telltale began negotiations with <a href="/wiki/Mojang" class="mw-redirect" title="Mojang">Mojang</a> in early 2013 and began work on the title shortly thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Stauffer noted that <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s acquisition of Mojang was not a factor in the game's development, as their interaction with Mojang began well before Microsoft's negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Telltale opted to create a new main character of Jesse for <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> instead of using default "<a href="/wiki/Steve_(Minecraft)" title="Steve (Minecraft)">Steve</a>" character from <i>Minecraft</i>, feeling that they did not want to attempt to rewrite how players already saw this character in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Other primary characters in the game are loosely designed around archetypes of common player-characters for <i>Minecraft</i>, such that those that engage in building, fighting, or griefing other players.<sup id="cite_ref-gamasutra_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The game did not attempt to provide any background for some concepts in <i>Minecraft</i>, such as the creepers, as to avoid the various interpretations that fans have done for these elements, though they are elements of the game's story.<sup id="cite_ref-gamasutra_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stauffer stated that the game's story would be aimed as <a href="/wiki/Family-friendly" title="Family-friendly">family-friendly</a>, similar to the films <i><a href="/wiki/The_Goonies" title="The Goonies">The Goonies</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Ghostbusters" title="Ghostbusters">Ghostbusters</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> their intended content would be equivalent to a <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Motion Picture Association of America">PG-13</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pan_European_Game_Information" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan European Game Information">PEGI</a>-12 rating.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_minecon_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_minecon-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gamasutra_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> A number of the voice actors are alumni of such films of the 1980s such as <a href="/wiki/Corey_Feldman" title="Corey Feldman">Corey Feldman</a> who starred in <i>The Goonies</i>, and the game includes various references to these types of films.<sup id="cite_ref-gamasutra_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Stauffer reflected that while Telltale's more recent games like <i>The Walking Dead</i> were more mature stories, their original adventure games like <i><a href="/wiki/Sam_%26_Max_Save_the_World" title="Sam &amp; Max Save the World">Sam &amp; Max</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Strong_Bad%27s_Cool_Game_for_Attractive_People" title="Strong Bad&#39;s Cool Game for Attractive People">Strong Bad's Cool Game for Attractive People</a></i> were written as family-friendly, and that they consider their approach to <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> as "part of our DNA".<sup id="cite_ref-eurogamer_firstlook_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogamer_firstlook-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The story was aimed to be accessible to both existing players of <i>Minecraft</i> – both novice and advanced players – and to new audiences outside of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> was formally announced in December 2014 as a collaboration project between Mojang and Telltale; the announcement was presented as an interactive adventure game named "Info Quest II".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Its first trailer was released during the <a href="/wiki/Minecon" title="Minecon">Minecon</a> 2015 convention in early July.<sup id="cite_ref-ign_trailer_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign_trailer-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The game was planned for a five-episode series for release on <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, iOS, Windows, OS X, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox" title="Xbox">Xbox</a> consoles in late 2015;<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Telltale also released the game for the <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a>, only a month after the original <i>Minecraft</i> first came to a <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> platform.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> It was also the first time a Telltale title had been released on a Nintendo platform since <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_The_Game" title="Back to the Future: The Game">Back to the Future: The Game</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-verge_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In addition, <i>Minecraft: Story Mode – The Complete Adventure</i>, incorporating both the main episodes and downloadable content, was announced for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Switch" title="Nintendo Switch">Nintendo Switch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The series released for most systems on October 13, 2015, with the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Vita" title="PlayStation Vita">PlayStation Vita</a> and Wii U versions to follow at a later date. A season pass of the game was available for purchase on October 27, 2015, which allows the player to access the other four episodes once they are released.<sup id="cite_ref-Episode_1_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Episode_1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Retail versions of the game were released on October 27, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Episode_2_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Episode_2-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> and Telltale signed a partnership in June 2018 for Netflix to offer Telltale's games over the service starting later that year, with <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> as the first planned title for the service.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Amid troubles related to the bankruptcy of Telltale Games in October and November 2018, sufficient staff remained with Telltale to complete work on this version, which was released onto Netflix on November 27 and December 5, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> It was removed on December 5, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_2">Season 2</span></h3>
<p>The first episode of <i>Minecraft: Story Mode – Season Two</i> was released on July 11, 2017, for Windows, macOS, PlayStation 4, Xbox 360, Xbox One, iOS and Android. It continued the story from the first season, with the player's choices affecting elements within <i>Season Two</i>. <a href="/wiki/Patton_Oswalt" title="Patton Oswalt">Patton Oswalt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Taber" title="Catherine Taber">Catherine Taber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Johnson_(actress)" title="Ashley Johnson (actress)">Ashley Johnson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Porter" title="Scott Porter">Scott Porter</a> were confirmed to continue voicework for the new season. The game supports the new Crowd Play feature that Telltale introduced in <i><a href="/wiki/Batman:_The_Telltale_Series" title="Batman: The Telltale Series">Batman: The Telltale Series</a></i>, allowing up to 2,000 audience members to vote on decisions for the player using <a href="/wiki/Twitch_(service)" title="Twitch (service)">Twitch</a> or other streaming services.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 3, 2017, Telltale announced that the second episode, "Giant Consequences", would be released on August 15.<sup id="cite_ref-S2-E2_twitter_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S2-E2_twitter-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The rest of the episodes were released on September 19, November 7,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and December 19, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Closure_of_Telltale_Games">Closure of Telltale Games</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telltale_Games#Majority_studio_closure_and_aftermath_(2018)" title="Telltale Games">Telltale Games §&#160;Majority studio closure and aftermath (2018)</a></div>
<p>In November 2018, Telltale Games began the process of closing down the studio due to financial issues. Most of its games started to become delisted from digital storefronts, including <i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i>. According to GOG.com, they had to pull the title due to "expiring licensing rights".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Minecraft</i> team stated that even for those that had purchased the titles before their delisting, the episodes would no longer be downloadable after June 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Because the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Live_Marketplace" class="mw-redirect" title="Xbox Live Marketplace">Xbox Live Marketplace</a> does not allow for removing games from sale while at the same time allowing existing owners to download the game, each episode of the game's Xbox 360 version was repriced to <span style="white-space: nowrap">$100</span> in the few weeks ahead of the delisting to deter users from purchasing them.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the closure of Telltale, Antimo, one of the game's composers, has stated that there is currently legal confusion as to where the rights to the soundtrack lies, leading to the soundtrack only being available for streaming on <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a> and <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>, where they were released before the closure of Telltale.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Soundtrack">Soundtrack</span></h2>
<p><i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> features an original soundtrack composed by American duo Antimo &amp; Welles, consisting of Skyler Barto (Antimo) and Andrew Arcadi (Welles). The soundtrack for the first season consists of 42 tracks, while the soundtrack for the second season has 51 tracks. On December 21, 2018, during the closure of Telltale, the duo released <i>Story Mode Archives</i>, an album consisting of 18 unused tracks from the game. Several more tracks were re-released in late 2021.
</p>

<p><i>Minecraft: Story Mode</i> received "mixed or average reviews" from critics, with the Nintendo Switch version earning a weighted average of 67 based on 5 critics.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Season_1_.282015.E2.80.9316.29_3"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_1_(2015–16)_3">Season 1 (2015–16)</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_1:_The_Order_of_the_Stone"><i>Episode 1: The Order of the Stone</i></span></h4>
<p>Aggregating review website <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> gave the Windows version 71/100 based on 25 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCPCEP1_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPCEP1-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> the PlayStation 4 version 71/100 based on 23 reviews<sup id="cite_ref-MCPS4EP1_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4EP1-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and the Xbox One version 77/100 based on 13 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCXONEEP1_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONEEP1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/GameRankings" title="GameRankings">GameRankings</a>, a score of 78.59% was given based on 11 reviews for the Xbox One version,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> 77.50% for Wii U based on 4 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> 73.53% for the PC version based on 16 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and 73.29% for PlayStation 4 based on 21 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_2:_Assembly_Required"><i>Episode 2: Assembly Required</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the Windows version 59/100 based on 13 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCPCEP2_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPCEP2-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> the PlayStation 4 version 53/100 based on 7 reviews<sup id="cite_ref-MCPS4EP2_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4EP2-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and the Xbox One version 61/100 based on 8 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCXONEEP2_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONEEP2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_3:_The_Last_Place_You_Look"><i>Episode 3: The Last Place You Look</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the Windows version 73/100 based on 10 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCPCEP3_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPCEP3-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> the PlayStation 4 version 73/100 based on 7 reviews<sup id="cite_ref-MCPS4EP3_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4EP3-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and the Xbox One version 75/100 based on 9 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCXONEEP3_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONEEP3-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_4:_A_Block_and_a_Hard_Place"><i>Episode 4: A Block and a Hard Place</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the Windows version 68/100 based on 8 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCPCEP4_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPCEP4-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> the PlayStation 4 version 72/100 based on 8 reviews<sup id="cite_ref-MCPS4EP4_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4EP4-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and the Xbox One version 71/100 based on 8 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCXONEEP4_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONEEP4-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Episode_5:_Order_Up.21"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_5:_Order_Up!"><i>Episode 5: Order Up!</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the Windows version 70/100 based on 6 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCPCEP5_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPCEP5-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> the PlayStation 4 version 72/100 based on 9 reviews<sup id="cite_ref-MCPS4EP5_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4EP5-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and the Xbox One version 69/100 based on 6 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCXONEEP5_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONEEP5-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_6:_A_Portal_to_Mystery"><i>Episode 6: A Portal to Mystery</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the Windows version 64/100 based on 5 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCPCEP6_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPCEP6-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> the PlayStation 4 version 69/100 based on 6 reviews<sup id="cite_ref-MCPS4EP6_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4EP6-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and the Xbox One version 71/100 based on 5 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCXONEEP6_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONEEP6-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_7:_Access_Denied"><i>Episode 7: Access Denied</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the Windows version 69/100 based on 4 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCPCEP7_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPCEP7-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> the PlayStation 4 version 68/100 based on 6 reviews<sup id="cite_ref-MCPS4EP7_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4EP7-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and the Xbox One version 71/100 based on 5 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCXONEEP7_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONEEP7-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Episode_8:_A_Journey.27s_End.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_8:_A_Journey's_End?"><i>Episode 8: A Journey's End?</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the PlayStation 4 version 69/100 based on 6 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCPS4EP8_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4EP8-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Season_2_.282017.29_3"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_2_(2017)_3">Season 2 (2017)</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_1:_Hero_in_Residence"><i>Episode 1: Hero in Residence</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the PC version 71/100 based on 8 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCSM_S2E1_MC_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCSM_S2E1_MC-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
the PlayStation 4 version 67/100 based on 8 reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-MCSM_S2E1_MC_PS4_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCSM_S2E1_MC_PS4-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
and the Xbox One version 76/100 based on 4 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-MCSM_S2E1_MC_X1_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCSM_S2E1_MC_X1-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_2:_Giant_Consequences"><i>Episode 2: Giant Consequences</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the PC version 74/100 based on 8 critics and<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> the PlayStation 4 version a score of 73/100 based on 4 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/GameRankings" title="GameRankings">GameRankings</a>, the PlayStation 4 version has a rating of 65.00% based on 2 reviews and on the PC version, it has a score of 72.86% based on 7 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_3:_Jailhouse_Block"><i>Episode 3: Jailhouse Block</i></span></h4>
<p>Metacritic gave the PC version 71/100, based on 8 reviews, and the PlayStation 4 63/100 based on 4 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_4:_Below_the_Bedrock"><i>Episode 4: Below the Bedrock</i></span></h4>
